Summary: 1. Primary Request and Intent: The user wants to get the game Celeste64 v1.1.0 (a .NET 8 self-contained macOS x64 application) running on their system: macOS 10.9.5 (Mavericks) on x86_64 hardware. The binary was built targeting macOS 10.15+ and requires many frameworks and system functions not available on 10.9. The user explicitly said "Do whatever it takes to get this game to run on this OS" and later directed "You're going to have to create inject compatibility libraries."

  1. Key Technical Concepts:
  2. Mach-O binary format: load commands (LC_LOAD_DYLIB, LC_LOAD_WEAK_DYLIB, LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY, LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS, LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE)
  3. DYLD environment variables: DYLD_FRAMEWORK_PATH, DYLD_LIBRARY_PATH, DYLD_FORCE_FLAT_NAMESPACE, DYLD_INSERT_LIBRARIES
  4. .NET 8 runtime: self-contained deployment, CoreCLR initialization, W^X (write-xor-execute) double mapping, ICU globalization
  5. Chained fixups format: pointer format 6 (DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64_OFFSET), rebase/bind chain walking, next field at bits 51-62 with stride 4
  6. Traditional Mach-O binding: rebase opcodes, bind opcodes, exports trie, LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
  7. Swift symbol mangling (_$s prefix symbols), Swift runtime functions
  8. macOS framework compatibility across versions (CryptoKit, Metal, CoreHaptics, Security framework constants)
  9. MacPorts Legacy Support library (/usr/local/lib/libMacportsLegacySupport.dylib) providing POSIX backports

  10. Fat/Universal binary handling with lipo

  17. /Users/Jonathan/Downloads/Celeste64-v1.1.0-macOS-x64/compat/patch_macho.c

    • Tool to convert Mach-O dylibs from chained fixups format to traditional LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY format
    • Parses dyld_chained_fixups_header, walks fixup chains, generates rebase/bind opcode streams
    • Key constant definitions (corrected): LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE = 0x80000033, LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS = 0x80000034
    • Chain walking uses next = ((raw >> 51) & 0xFFF) * 4 for both PTR_64 and PTR_64_OFFSET formats
    • Removes LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS, LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE, and LC_BUILD_VERSION commands
    • Adds LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY pointing to generated rebase/bind data appended at file end, plus the original exports trie
    • Successfully processed libFosterPlatform: 4360 rebases, 729 binds

  18. /Users/Jonathan/Downloads/Celeste64-v1.1.0-macOS-x64/libFosterPlatform.dylib

    • Original backed up to libFosterPlatform.dylib.bak
    • Currently replaced with libFosterPlatform_patched.dylib

  19. /Users/Jonathan/Downloads/Celeste64-v1.1.0-macOS-x64/libFosterPlatform_x64.dylib

    • The x86_64 slice extracted via lipo -thin x86_64

  20. Errors and fixes:

  21. CryptoKit version mismatch: Stub had version 0.0.0, binary required 1.0.0. Fixed by adding -compatibility_version 1.0.0 -current_version 1.0.0 to clang.
  22. Double-underscore symbol prefix: C compiler adds _ prefix, causing __$s9CryptoKit... instead of _$s9CryptoKit.... Fixed by using __asm__("exact_symbol_name") directives with unique C names.
  23. thread_read_t unknown type: 10.9 SDK uses thread_t instead. Changed parameter type to thread_t.
  24. mmap syscall truncation: syscall() returns int which truncates 64-bit pointers. First tried inline assembly (still crashed at bundle::reader_t), then fixed by calling extern void *__mmap() from libsystem_kernel directly.
  25. LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE/LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS constants swapped: Had 0x80000034 = EXPORTS_TRIE and 0x80000033 = FIXUPS, but correct values are 0x80000033 = EXPORTS_TRIE and 0x80000034 = FIXUPS. Discovered by checking actual data at file offsets - data at 0x1d0000 was a valid fixups header (version=0, imports_count=498).
  26. Wrong next field bit position in chained fixups: Tried bits 36-50 (15 bits), then bits 44-55 (12 bits), but correct position is bits 51-62 (12 bits) with stride 4. Verified by examining raw GOT entries where consecutive 8-byte entries should have next=8.
  27. No room for LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY: Space check compared against segment fileoff (0 for __TEXT) instead of first section offset (0x9de0). Fixed by scanning all sections to find the minimum section offset.
  28. User told us mp-nm exists: We were stuck because system nm couldn't parse the binary ("unknown load command 10"). User informed us that a modern nm is installed as mp-nm.

  29. User suggested MacPorts Legacy Support: We were manually implementing clock_gettime, fstatat, etc. User pointed out /usr/local/lib/libMacportsLegacySupport.dylib already has these symbols. Simplified our shim significantly.

  30. Problem Solving:

  48. Current Work: The patched libFosterPlatform.dylib is being rejected by dyld with "bad bind type 0". The Mach-O patcher (patch_macho.c) successfully converted 4360 rebases and 729 binds from chained fixups format to traditional LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY bind/rebase opcodes, but the bind opcode encoding has an issue. The error occurs during dlopen() of the library.

The bind opcode stream starts with BIND_OPCODE_SET_TYPE_IMM | BIND_TYPE_POINTER (0x51) followed by individual bind entries each containing: SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL, SET_SYMBOL_TRAILING_FLAGS_IMM + symbol name, SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB, DO_BIND. The "bad bind type 0" error suggests dyld isn't seeing the initial type-setting opcode, or there's an issue with how bind entries interact with lazy binding expectations.

The last output was: dlopen(/Users/Jonathan/Downloads/Celeste64-v1.1.0-macOS-x64/libFosterPlatform.dylib, 1): bad bind type 0 in /Users/Jonathan/Downloads/Celeste64-v1.1.0-macOS-x64/libFosterPlatform.dylib

The bind opcode stream generated by patch_macho.c needs investigation - likely the bind type needs to be set before each DO_BIND operation, or there's a need to separate regular binds from lazy binds (GOT entries vs stub helper entries), or the indirect symbol table entries need to be updated to match the new binding format. import struct
with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()
    # Find LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY (0x80000022 = 2147483682)
    off = 32  # after mach_header_64
    magic = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 0)[0]
    ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
    for i in range(ncmds):
        cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
        if cmd == 0x80000022:  # LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
            vals = struct.unpack_from('<IIIIIIIIIIIII', data, off)
            print(vals[3])  # bind_off
            break
        off += cmdsize
") libFosterPlatform.dylib 2>&1 | head -20

$ Bash
Parse Mach-O load commands to find LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY and section types
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

magic = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 0)[0]
print(f'Magic: 0x{magic:08x}')
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
sizeofcmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 20)[0]
print(f'ncmds={ncmds}, sizeofcmds={sizeofcmds}')

off = 32  # after mach_header_64
for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x80000022:  # LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
        vals = struct.unpack_from('<12I', data, off)
        print(f'LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY at offset {off}:')
        print(f'  cmd=0x{vals[0]:08x} cmdsize={vals[1]}')
        print(f'  rebase_off={vals[2]} rebase_size={vals[3]}')
        print(f'  bind_off={vals[4]} bind_size={vals[5]}')
        print(f'  weak_bind_off={vals[6]} weak_bind_size={vals[7]}')
        print(f'  lazy_bind_off={vals[8]} lazy_bind_size={vals[9]}')
        print(f'  export_off={vals[10]} export_size={vals[11]}')
        # Show first bytes of rebase data
        print(f'  Rebase data at {vals[2]}: {data[vals[2]:vals[2]+32].hex()}')
        print(f'  Bind data at {vals[4]}: {data[vals[4]:vals[4]+64].hex()}')
        if vals[10] > 0:
            print(f'  Export data at {vals[10]}: {data[vals[10]:vals[10]+32].hex()}')
    elif cmd == 0x19:  # LC_SEGMENT_64
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize = struct.unpack_from('<QQQQ', data, off+24)
        nsects = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, off+64)[0]
        print(f'  Segment {segname}: vmaddr=0x{vmaddr:x} fileoff=0x{fileoff:x} filesize=0x{filesize:x} nsects={nsects}')
        # Check for special section types  
        for j in range(nsects):
            soff = off + 80 + j * 80
            sectname = data[soff:soff+16].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            segn = data[soff+16:soff+32].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            s_addr, s_size, s_offset = struct.unpack_from('<QQI', data, soff+32)
            s_flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+64)[0]
            s_type = s_flags & 0xff
            if s_type in [6, 7, 8, 9, 0xa, 0xb]:  # symbol pointer/stub section types
                s_reserved1 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+68)[0]
                print(f'    Section {sectname} type=0x{s_type:x} flags=0x{s_flags:x} reserved1(indirect_idx)={s_reserved1} offset=0x{s_offset:x} size=0x{s_size:x}')
    elif cmd == 0xb:  # LC_DYSYMTAB
        vals = struct.unpack_from('<20I', data, off)
        print(f'LC_DYSYMTAB: indirectsymoff={vals[16]} nindirectsyms={vals[17]}')
    off += cmdsize
print(f'File size: {len(data)}')
"

import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:  # LC_SEGMENT_64
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize = struct.unpack_from('<QQQQ', data, off+24)
        nsects = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, off+64)[0]
        print(f'Segment {segname}: vmaddr=0x{vmaddr:x} nsects={nsects}')
        for j in range(nsects):
            soff = off + 80 + j * 80
            sectname = data[soff:soff+16].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            segn = data[soff+16:soff+32].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            s_addr, s_size, s_offset = struct.unpack_from('<QQI', data, soff+32)
            s_align = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+44)[0]
            s_reloff = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+48)[0]
            s_nreloc = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+52)[0]
            s_flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+56)[0]
            s_reserved1 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+60)[0]
            s_reserved2 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+64)[0]
            s_type = s_flags & 0xff
            type_names = {0:'S_REGULAR', 1:'S_ZEROFILL', 2:'S_CSTRING', 5:'S_LITERAL_PTRS',
                         6:'S_NON_LAZY_SYM_PTRS', 7:'S_LAZY_SYM_PTRS', 8:'S_SYMBOL_STUBS',
                         9:'S_MOD_INIT', 0xa:'S_MOD_TERM', 0xb:'S_COALESCED'}
            tn = type_names.get(s_type, f'0x{s_type:x}')
            print(f'  {sectname:20s} {segn:16s} addr=0x{s_addr:x} size=0x{s_size:x} off=0x{s_offset:x} flags=0x{s_flags:08x} type={tn} r1={s_reserved1} r2={s_reserved2}')
    off += cmdsize
"

Agent "Research chained fixups format" completed

All file and search tools are denied in this environment. However, I have deep knowledge of these Mach-O formats from my training data, which includes the Apple open-source headers and extensive reverse-engineering documentation. Here is a comprehensive reference covering all three areas you need.

1. LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS (Load Command 0x80000034)

Load Command

// In loader.h
#define LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS 0x80000034

struct linkedit_data_command {
    uint32_t cmd;       // LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS
    uint32_t cmdsize;   // sizeof(struct linkedit_data_command) = 16
    uint32_t dataoff;   // file offset of chained fixups data in __LINKEDIT
    uint32_t datasize;  // size of chained fixups data
};

Top-Level Header (at dataoff)

struct dyld_chained_fixups_header {
    uint32_t fixups_version;    // 0
    uint32_t starts_offset;     // offset of dyld_chained_starts_in_image in this data
    uint32_t imports_offset;    // offset of imports table in this data
    uint32_t symbols_offset;    // offset of symbol strings in this data
    uint32_t imports_count;     // number of imported symbol names
    uint32_t imports_format;    // DYLD_CHAINED_IMPORT, _IMPORT_ADDEND, or _IMPORT_ADDEND64
    uint32_t symbols_format;    // 0 => uncompressed, 1 => zlib compressed
};

Starts-in-Image (at fixups_header + starts_offset)

struct dyld_chained_starts_in_image {
    uint32_t seg_count;
    uint32_t seg_info_offset[];  // array of seg_count uint32_t offsets
    // Each offset is from the start of this struct to a dyld_chained_starts_in_segment.
    // An offset of 0 means that segment has no fixups.
};

Starts-in-Segment (at starts_in_image + seg_info_offset[i])

struct dyld_chained_starts_in_segment {
    uint32_t size;              // size of this struct (including variable-length page_start array)
    uint16_t page_size;         // 0x1000 or 0x4000
    uint16_t pointer_format;    // DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_* enum
    uint64_t segment_offset;    // offset of first fixup in segment (from mach_header)
    uint32_t max_valid_pointer; // for 32-bit, max valid pointer value (0 for 64-bit)
    uint16_t page_count;        // number of pages with fixups
    uint16_t page_start[];      // array of page_count entries
    // Each page_start value is the offset within that page of the first fixup,
    // or DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_START_NONE (0xFFFF) if no fixups on that page.
    // DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_START_MULTI (0x8000 bit set) means overflow entries follow.
};

Pointer Formats (pointer_format field)

The key formats you will encounter:

enum {
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_ARM64E                 =  1, // stride 8, unauth/auth targets
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64                     =  2, // stride 4, target is vmaddr
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_32                     =  3,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_32_CACHE              =  4,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_32_FIRMWARE           =  5,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64_OFFSET             =  6, // stride 4, target is offset from mach_header
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_ARM64E_KERNEL         =  7,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64_KERNEL_CACHE       =  8,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_ARM64E_USERLAND       =  9, // stride 8, target is offset from mach_header
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_ARM64E_FIRMWARE       = 10,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_X86_64_KERNEL_CACHE   = 11,
    DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_ARM64E_USERLAND24     = 12, // stride 8
};

#define DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_START_NONE  0xFFFF
#define DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_START_MULTI 0x8000

Chain Entry Formats (the actual pointer values in DATA pages)

For DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64 (format 2) -- the most common for x86_64 dylibs:

// Each 64-bit value at a fixup location is a union:
struct dyld_chained_ptr_64_rebase {
    uint64_t target   : 36,  // vmaddr (max 64GB)
             high8    :  8,  // top 8 bits of target vmaddr
             reserved :  7,
             next     : 12,  // offset to next fixup in units of 4 bytes (stride=4)
             bind     :  1;  // 0 => rebase
};

struct dyld_chained_ptr_64_bind {
    uint64_t ordinal  : 24,  // index into imports table
             addend   :  8,  // addend (signed)
             reserved : 19,
             next     : 12,  // offset to next in units of 4 bytes
             bind     :  1;  // 1 => bind
};

For DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64_OFFSET (format 6) -- also common for x86_64:

struct dyld_chained_ptr_64_rebase {
    uint64_t target   : 36,  // offset from mach_header (NOT vmaddr)
             high8    :  8,  // top 8 bits of the pointer value
             reserved :  7,
             next     : 12,  // stride = 4 bytes
             bind     :  1;  // 0 => rebase
};
// bind format is identical to DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_64

For DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_ARM64E_USERLAND (format 9) -- common for arm64e:

struct dyld_chained_ptr_arm64e_rebase {
    uint64_t target   : 34,  // offset from mach_header
             high8    :  8,
             next     : 11,  // stride = 8 bytes
             bind     :  1,  // 0
             auth     :  1;  // 0
             // bit 63 unused
};

struct dyld_chained_ptr_arm64e_bind {
    uint64_t ordinal  : 16,
             zero     : 16,
             addend   : 19,  // signed
             next     : 11,  // stride = 8
             bind     :  1,  // 1
             auth     :  1;  // 0
};

struct dyld_chained_ptr_arm64e_auth_rebase {
    uint64_t target    : 32, // offset from mach_header
             diversity : 16,
             addrDiv   :  1,
             key       :  2,
             next      : 11, // stride = 8
             bind      :  1, // 0
             auth      :  1; // 1
};

struct dyld_chained_ptr_arm64e_auth_bind {
    uint64_t ordinal   : 16,
             zero      : 16,
             diversity : 16,
             addrDiv   :  1,
             key       :  2,
             next      : 11,
             bind      :  1, // 1
             auth      :  1; // 1
};

Walking a Chain

Algorithm: 1. For each segment with seg_info_offset[i] != 0, read dyld_chained_starts_in_segment. 2. For each page where page_start[j] != DYLD_CHAINED_PTR_START_NONE: - Compute the address of the first fixup: segment_offset + (j * page_size) + page_start[j] - Read the 64-bit (or 32-bit) value at that file offset. - Check the bind bit to determine rebase vs bind. - Extract next. If next == 0, chain ends. Otherwise, advance by next * stride bytes to the next fixup.

Import Table Formats

At fixups_header + imports_offset, an array of imports_count entries:

// imports_format == 1 (DYLD_CHAINED_IMPORT)
struct dyld_chained_import {
    uint32_t lib_ordinal :  8,  // library ordinal (signed)
             weak_import :  1,
             name_offset : 23;  // offset in symbol string pool
};

// imports_format == 2 (DYLD_CHAINED_IMPORT_ADDEND)
struct dyld_chained_import_addend {
    uint32_t lib_ordinal :  8,
             weak_import :  1,
             name_offset : 23;
    int32_t  addend;
};

// imports_format == 3 (DYLD_CHAINED_IMPORT_ADDEND64)
struct dyld_chained_import_addend64 {
    uint64_t lib_ordinal : 16,
             weak_import :  1,
             reserved    : 15,
             name_offset : 32;
    uint64_t addend;
};

The lib_ordinal is a signed value: - 0 means self (this image) - -1 (0xFF as uint8) means main executable - -2 (0xFE) means flat lookup - -3 (0xFD) means weak lookup (try all loaded) - Positive values are 1-based indices into the LC_LOAD_DYLIB / LC_LOAD_WEAK_DYLIB commands

The symbol name is at fixups_header + symbols_offset + name_offset (null-terminated C string).

2. LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY (Load Command 0x80000022)

This is the traditional format you need to produce.

Load Command

#define LC_DYLD_INFO      0x22
#define LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY 0x80000022

struct dyld_info_command {
    uint32_t cmd;             // LC_DYLD_INFO or LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
    uint32_t cmdsize;         // sizeof(struct dyld_info_command) = 48
    uint32_t rebase_off;      // file offset of rebase info in __LINKEDIT
    uint32_t rebase_size;     // size of rebase info
    uint32_t bind_off;        // file offset of binding info
    uint32_t bind_size;       // size of binding info
    uint32_t weak_bind_off;   // file offset of weak binding info
    uint32_t weak_bind_size;
    uint32_t lazy_bind_off;   // file offset of lazy binding info
    uint32_t lazy_bind_size;
    uint32_t export_off;      // file offset of export info (trie)
    uint32_t export_size;     // size of export info
};

Rebase Opcodes

The rebase info is a bytecode stream. Each byte has a 4-bit opcode in the high nibble and a 4-bit immediate in the low nibble.

#define REBASE_TYPE_POINTER         1
#define REBASE_TYPE_TEXT_ABSOLUTE32  2
#define REBASE_TYPE_TEXT_PCREL32     3

// Opcodes (high 4 bits)
#define REBASE_OPCODE_MASK                             0xF0
#define REBASE_IMMEDIATE_MASK                          0x0F

#define REBASE_OPCODE_DONE                             0x00
#define REBASE_OPCODE_SET_TYPE_IMM                     0x10  // type = imm
#define REBASE_OPCODE_SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB      0x20  // seg_index = imm, offset = ULEB128
#define REBASE_OPCODE_ADD_ADDR_ULEB                    0x30  // offset += ULEB128
#define REBASE_OPCODE_ADD_ADDR_IMM_SCALED              0x40  // offset += imm * pointer_size
#define REBASE_OPCODE_DO_REBASE_IMM_TIMES              0x50  // do rebase imm times, each advancing by pointer_size
#define REBASE_OPCODE_DO_REBASE_ULEB_TIMES             0x60  // do rebase ULEB128 times
#define REBASE_OPCODE_DO_REBASE_ADD_ADDR_ULEB          0x70  // do 1 rebase, then offset += ULEB128 + pointer_size
#define REBASE_OPCODE_DO_REBASE_ULEB_TIMES_SKIPPING_ULEB 0x80 // rebase ULEB times, each skip ULEB bytes + ptr_size

ULEB128 encoding: Standard unsigned LEB128. Each byte contributes 7 bits; high bit means "more bytes follow."

Typical rebase stream you would emit:

SET_TYPE_IMM(REBASE_TYPE_POINTER)          // 0x11
SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB(seg, offset)   // 0x20 | seg, then ULEB128(offset)
DO_REBASE_IMM_TIMES(1)                     // 0x51  (rebase 1 pointer at current location)
ADD_ADDR_ULEB(skip)                        // 0x30, ULEB128(skip) -- to jump to next rebase
... repeat ...
DONE                                       // 0x00

Bind Opcodes

Similar bytecode format. The bind stream records external symbol references.

#define BIND_TYPE_POINTER                       1
#define BIND_TYPE_TEXT_ABSOLUTE32                2
#define BIND_TYPE_TEXT_PCREL32                   3

#define BIND_SPECIAL_DYLIB_SELF                  0
#define BIND_SPECIAL_DYLIB_MAIN_EXECUTABLE      -1
#define BIND_SPECIAL_DYLIB_FLAT_LOOKUP          -2
#define BIND_SPECIAL_DYLIB_WEAK_LOOKUP          -3

#define BIND_SYMBOL_FLAGS_WEAK_IMPORT           0x01
#define BIND_SYMBOL_FLAGS_NON_WEAK_DEFINITION   0x08

// Opcodes (high 4 bits)
#define BIND_OPCODE_DONE                               0x00
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_IMM              0x10  // ordinal = imm
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_ULEB             0x20  // ordinal = ULEB128
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_DYLIB_SPECIAL_IMM              0x30  // ordinal = sign-extended imm
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_SYMBOL_TRAILING_FLAGS_IMM      0x40  // flags = imm, then null-terminated symbol name
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_TYPE_IMM                       0x50  // type = imm
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_ADDEND_SLEB                    0x60  // addend = SLEB128
#define BIND_OPCODE_SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB        0x70  // seg = imm, offset = ULEB128
#define BIND_OPCODE_ADD_ADDR_ULEB                      0x80  // offset += ULEB128
#define BIND_OPCODE_DO_BIND                            0x90  // bind at current location, advance by ptr_size
#define BIND_OPCODE_DO_BIND_ADD_ADDR_ULEB              0xA0  // bind, then offset += ULEB128 + ptr_size
#define BIND_OPCODE_DO_BIND_ADD_ADDR_IMM_SCALED        0xB0  // bind, then offset += imm*ptr_size + ptr_size
#define BIND_OPCODE_DO_BIND_ULEB_TIMES_SKIPPING_ULEB   0xC0  // bind ULEB times, skip ULEB + ptr_size each
#define BIND_OPCODE_THREADED                           0xD0  // (newer, for chained fixups in bind stream)

SET_DYLIB_SPECIAL_IMM encoding: The immediate is sign-extended from 4 bits. So ordinal -1 is encoded as 0x30 | 0x0F = 0x3F. Ordinal -2 is 0x3E. Ordinal 0 is 0x30.

Typical bind stream for one symbol:

SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_IMM(ordinal)             // 0x10 | ordinal  (if ordinal fits in 4 bits)
SET_SYMBOL_TRAILING_FLAGS_IMM(flags)       // 0x40 | flags, followed by "symbol_name\0"
SET_TYPE_IMM(BIND_TYPE_POINTER)            // 0x51
SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB(seg, offset)   // 0x70 | seg, ULEB128(offset)
SET_ADDEND_SLEB(addend)                    // 0x60, SLEB128(addend)  -- only if addend != 0
DO_BIND                                    // 0x90

Weak Bind Info

Same opcode format as regular bind. Used for symbols with BIND_SYMBOL_FLAGS_WEAK_IMPORT or weak definitions. Goes in weak_bind_off/weak_bind_size.

Lazy Bind Info

Also same opcode format, but each lazy symbol's opcodes are self-contained (they start from scratch with SET_DYLIB, SET_SYMBOL, etc. and end with DONE). The __la_symbol_ptr section's entries contain offsets into the lazy bind area. Each stub jumps through the pointer, and the initial pointer value causes dyld_stub_binder to be called, which uses the offset to find the right lazy bind record.

For your converter, if the chained fixups dylib doesn't use lazy binding (many modern dylibs don't -- they use non-lazy binding for everything), you can put all binds in the regular bind section and leave lazy_bind empty.

3. Exports Trie (LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE vs embedded in LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY)

LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE

#define LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE 0x80000033

struct linkedit_data_command {
    uint32_t cmd;       // LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE
    uint32_t cmdsize;   // 16
    uint32_t dataoff;   // file offset of trie data in __LINKEDIT
    uint32_t datasize;  // size of trie data
};

The trie data format is identical whether it comes from LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE or from the export_off/export_size fields in LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY. The only difference is where the offset/size is specified.

Trie Binary Format

The trie is a byte-serialized prefix tree. Each node has:

node:
    ULEB128 terminal_size     // 0 if not a terminal (no exported symbol ends here)
    if terminal_size > 0:
        ULEB128 flags         // export flags
        if flags & EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_REEXPORT:
            ULEB128 ordinal   // dylib ordinal for re-export
            char[] name       // null-terminated imported name (or empty for same name)
        else if flags & EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_STUB_AND_RESOLVER:
            ULEB128 stub_offset    // offset of stub from mach_header
            ULEB128 resolver_offset
        else:
            ULEB128 symbol_offset  // offset from mach_header for regular exports
    uint8_t child_count       // number of child edges
    for each child:
        char[] edge_label     // null-terminated edge string (label characters)
        ULEB128 child_offset  // offset from start of trie data to child node

Export Flags

#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_KIND_MASK           0x03
#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_KIND_REGULAR        0x00
#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_KIND_THREAD_LOCAL   0x01
#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_KIND_ABSOLUTE       0x02

#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_WEAK_DEFINITION     0x04
#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_REEXPORT            0x08
#define EXPORT_SYMBOL_FLAGS_STUB_AND_RESOLVER   0x10

Conversion Strategy for Exports

Since the trie format is identical, your converter just needs to: 1. Read the trie data from wherever LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE points. 2. Copy it verbatim into the export_off/export_size region of your new LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY command. 3. Remove the LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE load command.

Conversion Strategy Summary

Here is the high-level algorithm for your converter:

Step 1: Parse the chained fixups

  • Read the linkedit_data_command for LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS.
  • Parse dyld_chained_fixups_header, then dyld_chained_starts_in_image.
  • For each segment, walk each page's chain.
  • For each fixup, check the bind bit:
  • bind=0 (rebase): Record (segment_index, offset_in_segment, target_vmaddr). For PTR_64_OFFSET, the target is mach_header_vmaddr + target_field.
  • bind=1 (bind): Look up the import by ordinal. Record (segment_index, offset_in_segment, lib_ordinal, symbol_name, addend).

Step 2: Generate rebase opcodes

  • Sort rebases by (segment_index, offset).
  • Emit SET_TYPE_IMM(POINTER).
  • For each rebase, emit SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB (if segment changed), then ADD_ADDR_ULEB or DO_REBASE_IMM_TIMES as appropriate.
  • Emit DONE.

Step 3: Generate bind opcodes

  • Group binds by (lib_ordinal, symbol_name), sorted by (segment_index, offset).
  • For each group, emit the dylib ordinal, symbol name, type, and then for each location emit segment/offset + DO_BIND.
  • Emit DONE.

Step 4: Fix the actual pointer values in DATA pages

This is critical. With chained fixups, the pointer slots in __DATA/__DATA_CONST contain the encoded chain entries (with next pointers, bind bits, etc.). With traditional rebase/bind: - Rebase locations: The pointer value should be the actual target virtual address (the runtime value before ASLR slide is applied). dyld will add the slide. - Bind locations: The pointer value should be 0 (dyld will fill in the resolved symbol address at load time).

Step 5: Rewrite load commands

  • Replace LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS with LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY.
  • Remove LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE (fold its data into the export_off/export_size of the new command).
  • Adjust __LINKEDIT segment size/offsets to accommodate the new rebase/bind/export data.
  • Update the sizeofcmds field in the mach_header.

Step 6: Patch __LINKEDIT

  • You will likely need to append the new rebase, bind, and export data to __LINKEDIT (or rewrite it entirely).
  • Update the __LINKEDIT segment's filesize/vmsize and the LC_SYMTAB/LC_DYSYMTAB offsets if they shift.

Important compatibility note for macOS 10.9

  • macOS 10.9's dyld understands LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY but not LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS or LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE.
  • You must also ensure the binary does not use any other features unsupported by 10.9's dyld (such as LC_BUILD_VERSION -- you may need to replace it with LC_VERSION_MIN_MACOSX).
  • The __DATA_CONST segment may need to be merged into __DATA, as older dyld versions may not handle it correctly. 1166811128663 Full transcript available at: /private/tmp/claude-501/-Users-Jonathan-Downloads-Celeste64-v1-1-0-macOS-x64/tasks/a93afe9b56a11caec.output

import struct

def dump_sections(filename):
    with open(filename,'rb') as f:
        data = f.read()
    
    magic = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 0)[0]
    ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
    print(f'=== {filename} === ncmds={ncmds}')
    
    off = 32
    for i in range(ncmds):
        cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
        if cmd == 0x19:  # LC_SEGMENT_64
            segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize = struct.unpack_from('<QQQQ', data, off+24)
            nsects = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, off+64)[0]
            print(f'Segment {segname}: vmaddr=0x{vmaddr:x} vmsize=0x{vmsize:x} fileoff=0x{fileoff:x} filesize=0x{filesize:x} nsects={nsects}')
            for j in range(nsects):
                soff = off + 80 + j * 80
                sectname = data[soff:soff+16].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
                segn = data[soff+16:soff+32].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
                s_addr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, soff+32)[0]
                s_size = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, soff+40)[0]
                s_offset = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+48)[0]
                s_align = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+52)[0]
                s_reloff = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+56)[0]
                s_nreloc = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+60)[0]
                s_flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+64)[0]
                s_reserved1 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+68)[0]
                s_reserved2 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+72)[0]
                s_type = s_flags & 0xff
                type_names = {0:'S_REGULAR', 1:'S_ZEROFILL', 2:'S_CSTRING', 5:'S_LITERAL_PTRS',
                             6:'S_NON_LAZY_SYM_PTRS', 7:'S_LAZY_SYM_PTRS', 8:'S_SYMBOL_STUBS',
                             9:'S_MOD_INIT', 0xa:'S_MOD_TERM', 0xb:'S_COALESCED',
                             0x12:'S_INIT_FUNC_OFFSETS', 0x13:'S_THREAD_LOCAL_VARIABLES'}
                tn = type_names.get(s_type, f'type_0x{s_type:x}')
                print(f'  {sectname:20s} {segn:16s} addr=0x{s_addr:08x} size=0x{s_size:06x} off=0x{s_offset:06x} flags=0x{s_flags:08x} {tn} r1={s_reserved1} r2={s_reserved2}')
        elif cmd == 0xb:  # LC_DYSYMTAB
            vals = struct.unpack_from('<20I', data, off)
            print(f'LC_DYSYMTAB: indirectsymoff=0x{vals[16]:x} nindirectsyms={vals[17]}')
        elif cmd == 0x80000022:  # LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
            vals = struct.unpack_from('<12I', data, off)
            print(f'LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY: rebase=0x{vals[2]:x}+{vals[3]} bind=0x{vals[4]:x}+{vals[5]} weak=0x{vals[6]:x}+{vals[7]} lazy=0x{vals[8]:x}+{vals[9]} export=0x{vals[10]:x}+{vals[11]}')
        elif cmd == 0x80000033:
            off2, sz = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off+8)
            print(f'LC_DYLD_EXPORTS_TRIE: off=0x{off2:x} size={sz}')
        elif cmd == 0x80000034:
            off2, sz = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off+8)
            print(f'LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS: off=0x{off2:x} size={sz}')
        off += cmdsize

dump_sections('libFosterPlatform.dylib')
print()

The section parsing has a bug - segment_command_64 header is 72 bytes, not 80. The sections were read at wrong offsets. Let me fix this.

Assistant2026-03-09T09:08:05.388Z
$ Bash
Re-dump sections with corrected 72-byte segment header offset
python3 -c "
import struct

def dump_sections(filename):
    with open(filename,'rb') as f:
        data = f.read()
    
    ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
    print(f'=== {filename} ===')
    
    off = 32
    for i in range(ncmds):
        cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
        if cmd == 0x19:  # LC_SEGMENT_64
            segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize = struct.unpack_from('<QQQQ', data, off+24)
            nsects = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, off+64)[0]
            print(f'Segment {segname}: vmaddr=0x{vmaddr:x} fileoff=0x{fileoff:x} filesize=0x{filesize:x} nsects={nsects}')
            for j in range(nsects):
                soff = off + 72 + j * 80  # segment_command_64 header is 72 bytes!
                sectname = data[soff:soff+16].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
                segn = data[soff+16:soff+32].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
                s_addr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, soff+32)[0]
                s_size = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, soff+40)[0]
                s_offset = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+48)[0]
                s_flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+64)[0]
                s_reserved1 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+68)[0]
                s_reserved2 = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, soff+72)[0]
                s_type = s_flags & 0xff
                type_names = {0:'S_REGULAR', 1:'S_ZEROFILL', 2:'S_CSTRING', 5:'S_LITERAL_PTRS',
                             6:'S_NON_LAZY_SYM_PTRS', 7:'S_LAZY_SYM_PTRS', 8:'S_SYMBOL_STUBS',
                             9:'S_MOD_INIT', 0xa:'S_MOD_TERM', 0xb:'S_COALESCED',
                             0x12:'S_INIT_FUNC_OFFSETS', 0x13:'S_THREAD_LOCAL_VARIABLES'}
                tn = type_names.get(s_type, f'type_0x{s_type:x}')
                print(f'  {sectname:24s} addr=0x{s_addr:08x} size=0x{s_size:06x} off=0x{s_offset:06x} flags=0x{s_flags:08x} {tn} r1={s_reserved1} r2={s_reserved2}')
        elif cmd == 0xb:  # LC_DYSYMTAB
            vals = struct.unpack_from('<20I', data, off)
            print(f'LC_DYSYMTAB: indirectsymoff=0x{vals[16]:x} nindirectsyms={vals[17]}')
        off += cmdsize

dump_sections('libFosterPlatform.dylib')
print()
dump_sections('libFosterPlatform_x64.dylib')

Assistant2026-03-09T09:09:20.893Z

Now I can see clearly. The __got section has type S_NON_LAZY_SYM_PTRS (0x06) and __stubs has type S_SYMBOL_STUBS (0x08). Both reference the indirect symbol table via reserved1, but nindirectsyms=0. When dyld on 10.9 sees these section types, it tries to bind them through the (empty) indirect symbol table, reading garbage.

The fix: change these section types to S_REGULAR so dyld doesn't try to use the indirect symbol table. Our bind opcodes already handle __got binding directly.

Assistant2026-03-09T09:09:28.031Z
$ Bash
Patch __got and __stubs section types to S_REGULAR to avoid indirect symbol table
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = bytearray(f.read())

off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        nsects = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, off+64)[0]
        for j in range(nsects):
            soff = off + 72 + j * 80
            sectname = data[soff:soff+16].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
            flags_off = soff + 64
            flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, flags_off)[0]
            s_type = flags & 0xff
            
            if sectname == '__got' and s_type == 0x06:
                new_flags = flags & ~0xff  # Clear type bits -> S_REGULAR
                struct.pack_into('<I', data, flags_off, new_flags)
                # Also clear reserved1 (indirect sym index)
                struct.pack_into('<I', data, soff+68, 0)
                print(f'Patched {sectname} flags: 0x{flags:08x} -> 0x{new_flags:08x}')
                
            if sectname == '__stubs' and s_type == 0x08:
                new_flags = flags & ~0xff  # Clear type bits -> S_REGULAR
                struct.pack_into('<I', data, flags_off, new_flags)
                struct.pack_into('<I', data, soff+68, 0)  # clear reserved1
                print(f'Patched {sectname} flags: 0x{flags:08x} -> 0x{new_flags:08x}')
    off += cmdsize

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','wb') as f:
    f.write(data)
print('Done')

Decode bind/rebase opcodes to find invalid segment indices
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

# Find LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x80000022:
        vals = struct.unpack_from('<12I', data, off)
        bind_off = vals[4]
        bind_size = vals[5]
        rebase_off = vals[2]
        rebase_size = vals[3]
        break
    off += cmdsize

def decode_uleb(data, pos):
    result = 0; shift = 0
    while pos < len(data):
        b = data[pos]; pos += 1
        result |= (b & 0x7F) << shift
        if not (b & 0x80): break
        shift += 7
    return result, pos

# Check rebase opcodes for segment indices
print('=== REBASE: checking segment indices ===')
pos = rebase_off
end = rebase_off + rebase_size
seg_indices_seen = set()
while pos < end:
    byte = data[pos]; pos += 1
    opcode = byte & 0xF0
    imm = byte & 0x0F
    if opcode == 0x00: break  # DONE
    elif opcode == 0x20:  # SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB
        if imm > 3:
            print(f'  REBASE segment {imm} at opcode offset {pos-1-rebase_off}')
        seg_indices_seen.add(imm)
        _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
    elif opcode == 0x30: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)  # ADD_ADDR_ULEB
    elif opcode == 0x60: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)  # DO_REBASE_ULEB_TIMES
    elif opcode == 0x70: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)  # DO_REBASE_ADD_ADDR_ULEB
    elif opcode == 0x80: 
        _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
        _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
print(f'Rebase segment indices: {sorted(seg_indices_seen)}')

# Check bind opcodes for segment indices
print('=== BIND: checking segment indices ===')
pos = bind_off
end = bind_off + bind_size
seg_indices_seen = set()
bad_segs = []
count = 0
while pos < end:
    byte = data[pos]; pos += 1
    opcode = byte & 0xF0
    imm = byte & 0x0F
    if opcode == 0x00: break
    elif opcode == 0x10: pass  # SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_IMM
    elif opcode == 0x20: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)  # SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_ULEB
    elif opcode == 0x30: pass  # SET_DYLIB_SPECIAL_IMM
    elif opcode == 0x40:  # SET_SYMBOL_TRAILING_FLAGS_IMM
        while pos < end and data[pos] != 0: pos += 1
        pos += 1  # skip null
    elif opcode == 0x50: pass  # SET_TYPE_IMM
    elif opcode == 0x60: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)  # SET_ADDEND_SLEB
    elif opcode == 0x70:  # SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB
        seg_indices_seen.add(imm)
        val, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
        if imm > 3:
            bad_segs.append((imm, val, count))
    elif opcode == 0x80: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
    elif opcode == 0x90: count += 1
    elif opcode == 0xA0: _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos); count += 1
    elif opcode == 0xB0: count += 1
    elif opcode == 0xC0:
        _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
        _, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos)
    else:
        print(f'Unknown opcode 0x{byte:02x} at offset {pos-1-bind_off}')
        break

print(f'Bind segment indices: {sorted(seg_indices_seen)}')
print(f'Total binds: {count}')
if bad_segs:
    print(f'BAD segments: {bad_segs[:5]}')
"

    data = f.read()

off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
bind_off = bind_size = 0
for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x80000022:
        vals = struct.unpack_from('<12I', data, off)
        bind_off = vals[4]; bind_size = vals[5]
        rebase_off = vals[2]; rebase_size = vals[3]
        weak_off = vals[6]; weak_size = vals[7]
        lazy_off = vals[8]; lazy_size = vals[9]
        print(f'bind_off=0x{bind_off:x} bind_size={bind_size}')
        print(f'rebase_off=0x{rebase_off:x} rebase_size={rebase_size}')
        print(f'weak_off=0x{weak_off:x} weak_size={weak_size}')
        print(f'lazy_off=0x{lazy_off:x} lazy_size={lazy_size}')
        break
    off += cmdsize

# Scan bind stream for any byte 0x75 (SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB | 5)
# But also trace through properly to find desync
def decode_uleb(data, pos, end):
    result = 0; shift = 0
    while pos < end:
        b = data[pos]; pos += 1
        result |= (b & 0x7F) << shift
        if not (b & 0x80): break
        shift += 7
    return result, pos

pos = bind_off
end = bind_off + bind_size
entry = 0
while pos < end:
    bpos = pos - bind_off
    byte = data[pos]; pos += 1
    opcode = byte & 0xF0
    imm = byte & 0x0F
    
    if opcode == 0x00:
        print(f'  [{bpos:5d}] DONE')
        break
    elif opcode == 0x10:
        pass  # SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_IMM
    elif opcode == 0x20:
        val, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
        if val > 0x7FFFFFFFFFFFFFFF:
            print(f'  [{bpos:5d}] SET_DYLIB_ORDINAL_ULEB val=0x{val:x} (HUGE - likely negative)')
    elif opcode == 0x30:
        pass  # SET_DYLIB_SPECIAL_IMM
    elif opcode == 0x40:
        sym_start = pos
        while pos < end and data[pos] != 0: pos += 1
        pos += 1  # skip null
    elif opcode == 0x50:
        pass  # SET_TYPE_IMM
    elif opcode == 0x60:
        val, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
    elif opcode == 0x70:
        val, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
        if imm > 3:
            print(f'  [{bpos:5d}] SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET seg={imm} off=0x{val:x} *** BAD ***')
    elif opcode == 0x80:
        val, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
    elif opcode == 0x90:
        entry += 1
    elif opcode == 0xA0:
        val, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
        entry += 1
    elif opcode == 0xB0:
        entry += 1
    elif opcode == 0xC0:
        val1, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
        val2, pos = decode_uleb(data, pos, end)
    else:
        print(f'  [{bpos:5d}] UNKNOWN opcode 0x{byte:02x}')
        # Show context
        ctx_start = max(bind_off, pos - 10)
        print(f'    Context: {data[ctx_start:pos+10].hex()}')
        break

print(f'Parsed {entry} bind entries, stream ok')
print(f'Remaining bytes after DONE: {end - pos}')

# Also check: is there a 0x75 byte anywhere in the bind data?
raw_bind = data[bind_off:bind_off+bind_size]
indices = [i for i, b in enumerate(raw_bind) if b == 0x75]
print(f'Occurrences of 0x75 in bind data: {len(indices)} (first 5: {indices[:5]})')
"

Assistant2026-03-09T09:13:44.759Z

Found the real issue. The rebase/bind data was appended past the end of __LINKEDIT but the segment's filesize/vmsize weren't updated. dyld maps __LINKEDIT and reads bind data from mapped memory - our data falls outside the mapped region.

__LINKEDIT ends at 0x1d0000 + 0x46228 = 0x216228, but bind data is at 0x21AEF8. dyld reads garbage, sees "segment 5".

Assistant2026-03-09T09:13:53.729Z
$ Bash
Extend __LINKEDIT segment to cover appended rebase/bind data
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = bytearray(f.read())

off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
linkedit_off = None
bind_end = 0

for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:  # LC_SEGMENT_64
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        if segname == '__LINKEDIT':
            linkedit_off = off
            vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+24)[0]
            vmsize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+32)[0]
            fileoff = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+40)[0]
            filesize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+48)[0]
            print(f'__LINKEDIT: vmaddr=0x{vmaddr:x} vmsize=0x{vmsize:x} fileoff=0x{fileoff:x} filesize=0x{filesize:x}')
    elif cmd == 0x80000022:
        vals = struct.unpack_from('<12I', data, off)
        rebase_off = vals[2]; rebase_size = vals[3]
        bind_off = vals[4]; bind_size = vals[5]
        export_off = vals[10]; export_size = vals[11]
        bind_end = max(bind_off + bind_size, rebase_off + rebase_size, export_off + export_size)
        print(f'Max data end: 0x{bind_end:x} (bind ends at 0x{bind_off+bind_size:x})')
    off += cmdsize

if linkedit_off:
    fileoff = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, linkedit_off+40)[0]
    # New filesize needs to cover all data
    new_filesize = bind_end - fileoff
    new_vmsize = (new_filesize + 0xFFF) & ~0xFFF  # Page-align vmsize
    
    old_filesize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, linkedit_off+48)[0]
    old_vmsize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, linkedit_off+32)[0]
    
    print(f'Updating __LINKEDIT:')
    print(f'  filesize: 0x{old_filesize:x} -> 0x{new_filesize:x}')
    print(f'  vmsize: 0x{old_vmsize:x} -> 0x{new_vmsize:x}')
    
    struct.pack_into('<Q', data, linkedit_off+32, new_vmsize)
    struct.pack_into('<Q', data, linkedit_off+48, new_filesize)
    
    with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','wb') as f:
        f.write(data)
    print('Done')
"

Verify rebased pointer values in __objc_selrefs
python3 -c "
import struct

# Check rebased pointers in __objc_selrefs section of patched binary
with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

# __objc_selrefs: addr=0x1c6ff0 size=0x14a8 off=0x1c6ff0
selrefs_off = 0x1c6ff0
selrefs_size = 0x14a8
nptrs = selrefs_size // 8

# Also check __objc_methname: addr=0x1b3f3f size=0x4a60  
methname_start = 0x1b3f3f
methname_end = 0x1b3f3f + 0x4a60

print(f'Checking {nptrs} selref pointers:')
bad = 0
for i in range(min(nptrs, 20)):  # first 20
    ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, selrefs_off + i * 8)[0]
    if ptr == 0:
        print(f'  [{i}] NULL pointer!')
        bad += 1
    elif methname_start <= ptr < methname_end:
        # Valid - read the string
        stroff = ptr  # ptr is vmaddr, which equals file offset for __TEXT
        s = data[stroff:stroff+50].split(b'\x00')[0].decode('ascii', errors='replace')
        print(f'  [{i}] 0x{ptr:x} -> \"{s}\"')
    else:
        # Check if ptr makes sense at all
        if ptr < len(data):
            s = data[ptr:ptr+30].split(b'\x00')[0].decode('ascii', errors='replace')
            print(f'  [{i}] 0x{ptr:x} (outside methname, data=\"{s}\")')
        else:
            print(f'  [{i}] 0x{ptr:x} (OUT OF FILE!)')
            bad += 1

# Count all bad ones
total_bad = 0
total_null = 0
for i in range(nptrs):
    ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, selrefs_off + i * 8)[0]
    if ptr == 0: total_null += 1
    elif ptr >= len(data): total_bad += 1
print(f'\\nTotal: {nptrs} ptrs, {total_null} NULL, {total_bad} out of file range')

# Also check the original binary's selrefs
with open('libFosterPlatform_x64.dylib','rb') as f:
    orig = f.read()

print(f'\\n=== Original binary first 5 selref raw values ===')
for i in range(5):
    raw = struct.unpack_from('<Q', orig, selrefs_off + i * 8)[0]
    bind = (raw >> 63) & 1
    if bind:
        ordinal = raw & 0xFFFFFF
        next_val = ((raw >> 51) & 0xFFF) * 4
        print(f'  [{i}] BIND ordinal={ordinal} next={next_val}')
    else:
        target = raw & 0xFFFFFFFFF  # 36 bits for PTR_64_OFFSET
        high8 = (raw >> 36) & 0xFF
        next_val = ((raw >> 51) & 0xFFF) * 4
        print(f'  [{i}] REBASE target=0x{target:x} high8=0x{high8:x} next={next_val} -> vmaddr=0x{((high8<<56)|target):x}')
"

import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

# Check __objc_classlist pointers
# __objc_classlist: addr=0x1c1a98 size=0x88
classlist_off = 0x1c1a98
classlist_size = 0x88
nclasses = classlist_size // 8
print(f'=== __objc_classlist ({nclasses} entries) ===')
for i in range(nclasses):
    ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, classlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    # Class pointer should point into __objc_data section 
    # __objc_data: addr=0x1c89b8 size=0x550
    if 0x1c89b8 <= ptr < 0x1c89b8 + 0x550:
        # Read class_ro_t pointer (at offset 32 in class structure)
        if ptr + 40 <= len(data):
            class_ro = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, ptr + 32)[0]
            if class_ro + 24 <= len(data):
                name_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, class_ro + 24)[0]
                if 0 < name_ptr < len(data):
                    name = data[name_ptr:name_ptr+40].split(b'\x00')[0].decode('ascii',errors='replace')
                    print(f'  [{i}] class at 0x{ptr:x} ro=0x{class_ro:x} name=\"{name}\"')
                else:
                    print(f'  [{i}] class at 0x{ptr:x} ro=0x{class_ro:x} BAD name_ptr=0x{name_ptr:x}')
            else:

The crashing pointer 0x00036a77000451b0 looks like an un-decoded chained fixup entry. Some fixup chains weren't properly walked. Let me investigate.


Assistant2026-03-09T09:18:54.224Z




$ Bash


Find un-decoded chained fixup entries in patched binary
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    patched = f.read()
with open('libFosterPlatform_x64.dylib','rb') as f:
    orig = f.read()

# Search for the crash pointer value in patched binary
crash_ptr = 0x00036a77000451b0
# Actually, search for any pointer in __objc_const that looks like a chained fixup
# A chained fixup entry has: bits 44-62 = next field (non-zero), bits 35-42 high8, target in low 36 bits
# Most legitimate vmaddrs would be < 0x200000 for this dylib
# Chained fixup values tend to have high bits set due to next/high8 fields

# Check __objc_const: addr=0x1c4000, size=0x2ff0
objc_const_off = 0x1c4000
objc_const_size = 0x2ff0

suspect = 0
print('=== Suspicious pointers in __objc_const (patched) ===')
for i in range(objc_const_size // 8):
    off = objc_const_off + i * 8
    val = struct.unpack_from('<Q', orig, off)[0]
    patched_val = struct.unpack_from('<Q', patched, off)[0]
    # Check if patched value still looks like a chained fixup
    # (has bits set above bit 35 that aren't a valid pointer)
    if patched_val > 0x200000 and patched_val != 0:
        # Could be valid if it's a large constant, but likely suspicious
        if patched_val > 0x0000FFFFFFFFFFFF:  # Very clearly not a valid pointer
            suspect += 1
            if suspect <= 10:
                print(f'  off=0x{off:x}: patched=0x{patched_val:016x} orig=0x{val:016x}')
                # Decode as chained fixup
                bind = (val >> 63) & 1
                next_v = ((val >> 51) & 0xFFF) * 4
                if bind:
                    ordinal = val & 0xFFFFFF
                    print(f'    -> BIND ordinal={ordinal} next={next_v}')
                else:
                    target = val & 0xFFFFFFFFF
                    high8 = (val >> 36) & 0xFF
                    print(f'    -> REBASE target=0x{target:x} high8=0x{high8:x} next={next_v}')

print(f'Total suspicious: {suspect}')

# Also check how many 8-byte values differ between orig and patched in DATA segments
total_diff = 0
same_raw = 0
for off in range(0x1bc000, 0x1d0000, 8):
    if off + 8 > len(orig) or off + 8 > len(patched): break

Find and categorize un-decoded chained fixup entries
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    patched = f.read()
with open('libFosterPlatform_x64.dylib','rb') as f:
    orig = f.read()

# Find unchanged high-bit values in DATA segments
unchanged_fixups = []
for off in range(0x1bc000, 0x1d0000, 8):
    if off + 8 > len(orig) or off + 8 > len(patched): break
    orig_val = struct.unpack_from('<Q', orig, off)[0]
    patched_val = struct.unpack_from('<Q', patched, off)[0]
    if orig_val == patched_val and orig_val != 0:
        # Check if it looks like a chained fixup (has next or high8 bits set above bit 35)
        bind = (orig_val >> 63) & 1
        next_v = ((orig_val >> 51) & 0xFFF) * 4
        if bind:
            ordinal = orig_val & 0xFFFFFF
            if next_v > 0 or ordinal < 1000:  # looks like a fixup
                unchanged_fixups.append((off, orig_val, 'BIND', ordinal, next_v))
        else:
            target = orig_val & 0xFFFFFFFFF
            high8 = (orig_val >> 36) & 0xFF
            reserved = (orig_val >> 44) & 0x7F
            # Valid vmaddr for this binary would be < 0x200000
            # Chained fixup would have non-zero next or bits above 36
            if next_v > 0 or high8 > 0 or reserved > 0:
                # But filter out values that are clearly not fixups
                # (e.g., constant data with specific patterns)
                unchanged_fixups.append((off, orig_val, 'REBASE?', target, next_v))

print(f'Found {len(unchanged_fixups)} potential un-decoded fixups:')
# Group by section
sections = {
    '__got': (0x1bc000, 0x1bcda8),
    '__const_dc': (0x1bcdb0, 0x1c0858),
    '__cfstring': (0x1c0858, 0x1c1a98),
    '__objc_classlist': (0x1c1a98, 0x1c1b20),
    '__objc_const': (0x1c4000, 0x1c6ff0),
    '__objc_selrefs': (0x1c6ff0, 0x1c8498),
    '__objc_classrefs': (0x1c8498, 0x1c86b0),
    '__objc_superrefs': (0x1c86b0, 0x1c86f8),
    '__objc_ivar': (0x1c86f8, 0x1c89b8),
    '__objc_data': (0x1c89b8, 0x1c8f08),
    '__data': (0x1c8fb0, 0x1ce108),
}
for sname, (start, end) in sections.items():
    entries = [(off,val,ty,a,b) for off,val,ty,a,b in unchanged_fixups if start <= off < end]
    if entries:
        print(f'  {sname}: {len(entries)} entries')
        for off, val, ty, a, b in entries[:3]:
            print(f'    0x{off:x}: 0x{val:016x} {ty} target/ord={a} next={b}')

# Show the specific crash value
crash_val = 0x00036a77000451b0
found = False
for off in range(0x1bc000, 0x1d0000, 8):
    if off + 8 > len(patched): break
    v = struct.unpack_from('<Q', patched, off)[0]
    if v == crash_val:
        print(f'\\nCrash value 0x{crash_val:x} found at offset 0x{off:x}')
        found = True
if not found:
    print(f'\\nCrash value 0x{crash_val:x} not found in DATA segments')
"

Count all fixup entries in original binary to verify completeness
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform_x64.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

# Parse chained fixups
off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
fixups_off = fixups_size = 0
segs = []

for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:  # LC_SEGMENT_64
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize = struct.unpack_from('<QQQQ', data, off+24)
        segs.append({'name': segname, 'vmaddr': vmaddr, 'fileoff': fileoff, 'filesize': filesize})
    elif cmd == 0x80000034:  # LC_DYLD_CHAINED_FIXUPS
        vals = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off+8)
        fixups_off = vals[0]
        fixups_size = vals[1]
    off += cmdsize

# Parse fixups header
cfh = struct.unpack_from('<7I', data, fixups_off)
starts_off = cfh[1]
imports_off = cfh[2]
symbols_off = cfh[3]
imports_count = cfh[4]
imports_format = cfh[5]

print(f'Fixups: imports={imports_count}, format={imports_format}')

# Parse starts_in_image
starts_base = fixups_off + starts_off
seg_count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, starts_base)[0]
print(f'seg_count={seg_count}, actual segments={len(segs)}')

seg_info_offsets = []
for i in range(seg_count):
    sio = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, starts_base + 4 + i * 4)[0]
    seg_info_offsets.append(sio)
    print(f'  seg {i} ({segs[i][\"name\"] if i < len(segs) else \"?\"}): info_offset={sio}')

# Walk chains in each segment
total_rebases = 0
total_binds = 0
for si in range(seg_count):
    if seg_info_offsets[si] == 0: continue
    if si >= len(segs): 
        print(f'  Seg {si}: no segment data!')
        continue
    
    ss_base = starts_base + seg_info_offsets[si]
    ss_size = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, ss_base)[0]
    page_size = struct.unpack_from('<H', data, ss_base + 4)[0]
    ptr_format = struct.unpack_from('<H', data, ss_base + 6)[0]
    seg_offset = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, ss_base + 8)[0]
    max_valid = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, ss_base + 16)[0]
    page_count = struct.unpack_from('<H', data, ss_base + 20)[0]
    
    seg_rebases = 0
    seg_binds = 0
    
    for pg in range(page_count):
        ps = struct.unpack_from('<H', data, ss_base + 22 + pg * 2)[0]
        if ps == 0xFFFF: continue
        
        off_in_seg = pg * page_size + ps
        while True:
            file_pos = segs[si]['fileoff'] + off_in_seg
            raw = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, file_pos)[0]
            bind = (raw >> 63) & 1
            next_v = ((raw >> 51) & 0xFFF) * 4
            
            if bind:
                seg_binds += 1
            else:
                seg_rebases += 1
            
            if next_v == 0: break
            off_in_seg += next_v
    
    total_rebases += seg_rebases
    total_binds += seg_binds
    print(f'  Seg {si} ({segs[si][\"name\"]}): fmt={ptr_format} pages={page_count} rebases={seg_rebases} binds={seg_binds}')

print(f'\\nTotal: {total_rebases} rebases, {total_binds} binds, {total_rebases+total_binds} fixups')
"

Assistant2026-03-09T09:22:19.217Z


Found it! The method lists use the relative/small method list format (flag 0x80000000), which was introduced in macOS 10.14+. The 10.9 ObjC runtime doesn't understand this format and reads garbage pointers. I need to convert all relative method lists to absolute format.


Assistant2026-03-09T09:22:30.473Z




$ Bash


Count method lists and space needed for conversion
python3 -c "
import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = f.read()

# __objc_methlist: addr=0x182820 size=0xd04
methlist_off = 0x182820
methlist_end = 0x182820 + 0xd04

# Scan all method lists
pos = methlist_off
total_methods = 0
total_lists = 0
while pos < methlist_end - 8:
    flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, pos)[0]
    count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, pos+4)[0]
    is_small = flags & 0x80000000
    entry_size = 12 if is_small else 24
    
    if count == 0 or count > 1000:
        pos += 4
        continue
    
    list_size = 8 + count * entry_size
    if pos + list_size > methlist_end:
        break
    
    total_lists += 1
    total_methods += count
    
    if total_lists <= 3 or not is_small:
        fmt = 'SMALL' if is_small else 'LARGE'
        print(f'Method list at 0x{pos:x}: {fmt} flags=0x{flags:x} count={count} size={list_size}')
    
    pos += list_size
    # Align to 4 bytes
    pos = (pos + 3) & ~3

print(f'\\nTotal: {total_lists} method lists, {total_methods} methods')
print(f'Space needed for absolute format: {8 + total_methods * 24} bytes (from {8 + total_methods * 12} original)')

# Also find all class_ro_t->baseMethods references to verify
off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    off += cmdsize

# Scan __objc_const for method list pointers
objc_const_off = 0x1c4000
objc_const_size = 0x2ff0
method_ptrs = set()
for offset in range(objc_const_off, objc_const_off + objc_const_size, 8):
    val = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, offset)[0]
    if methlist_off <= val < methlist_end:
        method_ptrs.add(val)

print(f'\\nDistinct method list addresses referenced: {len(method_ptrs)}')
for mp in sorted(method_ptrs)[:5]:
    flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, mp)[0]
    count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, mp+4)[0]
    is_small = flags & 0x80000000
    print(f'  0x{mp:x}: flags=0x{flags:x} count={count} {\"SMALL\" if is_small else \"LARGE\"}')
"

import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = bytearray(f.read())

# Find __LINKEDIT segment info
off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
linkedit_cmd_off = None
linkedit_vmaddr = linkedit_fileoff = linkedit_filesize = linkedit_vmsize = 0

for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        if segname == '__LINKEDIT':
            linkedit_cmd_off = off
            linkedit_vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+24)[0]
            linkedit_vmsize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+32)[0]
            linkedit_fileoff = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+40)[0]
            linkedit_filesize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+48)[0]
    off += cmdsize

print(f'__LINKEDIT: vmaddr=0x{linkedit_vmaddr:x} fileoff=0x{linkedit_fileoff:x} filesize=0x{linkedit_filesize:x}')

# Align to 8 bytes for new method list data
new_data_fileoff = (len(data) + 7) & ~7
padding = new_data_fileoff - len(data)
data.extend(b'\x00' * padding)

# __objc_methlist section info
methlist_off = 0x182820
methlist_end = methlist_off + 0xd04

# Scan __objc_const for all class_ro_t baseMethods pointers
# class_ro_t layout: flags(4), iStart(4), iSize(4), reserved(4), ivarLayout(8), name(8), baseMethods(8@+32), ...
# We need to find all class_ro_t structures. They're pointed to from class structures.
# Class structures are in __objc_data (0x1c89b8) and pointed to from __objc_classlist (0x1c1a98)

classlist_off = 0x1c1a98
classlist_size = 0x88
nclasses = classlist_size // 8

# Collect all (class_ro_offset, baseMethods_offset, old_methods_addr) pairs
fixups = []
for i in range(nclasses):
    class_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, classlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    if class_ptr == 0 or class_ptr >= len(data): continue
    
    # Process both class and metaclass
    for label in ['class', 'meta']:
        if label == 'meta':
            class_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, class_ptr)[0]  # isa = metaclass
            if class_ptr == 0 or class_ptr >= len(data): break
        
        ro_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, class_ptr + 32)[0]
        if ro_ptr == 0 or ro_ptr >= len(data): continue
        
        methods_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, ro_ptr + 32)[0]
        if methods_ptr == 0 or methods_ptr >= len(data): continue
        
        # Check if this is a small method list
        flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_ptr)[0]
        if flags & 0x80000000:
            fixups.append((ro_ptr, ro_ptr + 32, methods_ptr))

# Also check category method lists 
# __objc_catlist: 0x1c1b20 size 0x8
catlist_off = 0x1c1b20
catlist_size = 0x8
for i in range(catlist_size // 8):
    cat_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, catlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    if cat_ptr == 0 or cat_ptr >= len(data): continue
    # category_t: name(8), cls(8), instanceMethods(8@+16), classMethods(8@+24), protocols(8@+32), instanceProperties(8@+40)
    for moff_in_cat in [16, 24]:
        methods_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, cat_ptr + moff_in_cat)[0]
        if methods_ptr == 0 or methods_ptr >= len(data): continue
        flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_ptr)[0]
        if flags & 0x80000000:
            fixups.append((cat_ptr, cat_ptr + moff_in_cat, methods_ptr))

print(f'Found {len(fixups)} method list references to convert')

# Convert each method list
new_methods_map = {}  # old_addr -> new_vmaddr
current_offset = new_data_fileoff

for ro_off, ptr_off, old_ml_addr in fixups:
    if old_ml_addr in new_methods_map:
        # Already converted, just update pointer
        struct.pack_into('<Q', data, ptr_off, new_methods_map[old_ml_addr])
        continue
    
    flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, old_ml_addr)[0]
    count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, old_ml_addr + 4)[0]
    
    # Build absolute method list
    new_flags = flags & ~0x80000000  # Clear small method list flag
    new_ml = struct.pack('<II', new_flags, count)
    
    for j in range(count):
        entry_base = old_ml_addr + 8 + j * 12
        sel_rel = struct.unpack_from('<i', data, entry_base)[0]  # signed
        types_rel = struct.unpack_from('<i', data, entry_base + 4)[0]
        imp_rel = struct.unpack_from('<i', data, entry_base + 8)[0]
        
        # Compute absolute addresses
        sel_ref_addr = entry_base + sel_rel  # points to selref entry
        types_addr = entry_base + 4 + types_rel  # points to types string
        imp_addr = entry_base + 8 + imp_rel  # points to implementation
        
        # Read the selector name from the selref (get the pointer to the name string)
        if 0 < sel_ref_addr < len(data) - 8:
            name_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, sel_ref_addr)[0]
        else:
            print(f'  WARNING: bad selref addr 0x{sel_ref_addr:x}')
            name_ptr = 0
        
        new_ml += struct.pack('<QQQ', name_ptr, types_addr, imp_addr)
    
    # Pad to 8-byte alignment
    while len(new_ml) % 8 != 0:
        new_ml += b'\x00'
    
    # Calculate vmaddr for this new method list
    new_vmaddr = linkedit_vmaddr + (current_offset - linkedit_fileoff)
    new_methods_map[old_ml_addr] = new_vmaddr
    
    # Append to data
    data.extend(new_ml)
    
    # Update the pointer in class_ro_t (or category)
    struct.pack_into('<Q', data, ptr_off, new_vmaddr)
    
    name_str = ''
    if count > 0:
        entry0 = old_ml_addr + 8
        sr = struct.unpack_from('<i', data, entry0)[0]
        sra = entry0 + sr
        if 0 < sra < len(data) - 8:
            np = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, sra)[0]
            if 0 < np < len(data):
                name_str = data[np:np+25].split(b'\x00')[0].decode('ascii',errors='replace')
    
    print(f'  ML @0x{old_ml_addr:x} ({count} methods, first: {name_str}) -> vmaddr 0x{new_vmaddr:x}')
    current_offset += len(new_ml)

# Update __LINKEDIT segment to cover new data
new_filesize = len(data) - linkedit_fileoff
new_vmsize = (new_filesize + 0xFFF) & ~0xFFF
struct.pack_into('<Q', data, linkedit_cmd_off + 32, new_vmsize)  # vmsize
struct.pack_into('<Q', data, linkedit_cmd_off + 48, new_filesize)  # filesize
print(f'\nUpdated __LINKEDIT: filesize=0x{new_filesize:x} vmsize=0x{new_vmsize:x}')

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(data)
print(f'Wrote {len(data)} bytes')
PYEOF

import struct

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib','rb') as f:
    data = bytearray(f.read())

# Find LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY and __LINKEDIT info
off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
di_off = None
linkedit_cmd_off = None
linkedit_vmaddr = linkedit_fileoff = 0
segs = []  # (name, vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize)

for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+24)[0]
        vmsize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+32)[0]
        fileoff = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+40)[0]
        filesize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+48)[0]
        segs.append((segname, vmaddr, vmsize, fileoff, filesize))
        if segname == '__LINKEDIT':
            linkedit_cmd_off = off
            linkedit_vmaddr = vmaddr
            linkedit_fileoff = fileoff
    elif cmd == 0x80000022:
        di_off = off
        di_vals = list(struct.unpack_from('<12I', data, off))
        # [cmd, cmdsize, rebase_off, rebase_size, bind_off, bind_size, 
        #  weak_off, weak_size, lazy_off, lazy_size, export_off, export_size]
    off += cmdsize

old_rebase_off = di_vals[2]
old_rebase_size = di_vals[3]
print(f'Old rebase: off=0x{old_rebase_off:x} size={old_rebase_size}')

# Read old rebase data
old_rebase = data[old_rebase_off:old_rebase_off + old_rebase_size]

# Find all new method list pointers that need rebasing
# They're in the __LINKEDIT area, after the original end
# Find method lists by scanning for updated class_ro_t baseMethods pointing into __LINKEDIT

# Actually, let me just find all method list data I added
# The new method lists start after the bind data
# Method lists are at vmaddrs starting from around 0x224688
# In the file, they start at some offset past the original data

# Find all absolute method list entries in the file
# Each absolute method list: flags(4), count(4), then count * [name(8), types(8), imp(8)]
# We know they're in the __LINKEDIT extended area

# First, find all class_ro_t baseMethods that point into __LINKEDIT vmaddr range
classlist_off = 0x1c1a98
classlist_size = 0x88
nclasses = classlist_size // 8

new_rebase_entries = []  # (segment_index, offset_in_segment) tuples

# Determine which segment the new method lists are in
# They're in __LINKEDIT (segment 3)
seg_idx = 3  # __LINKEDIT

for i in range(nclasses):
    class_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, classlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    if class_ptr == 0 or class_ptr >= len(data): continue
    
    for label in ['class', 'meta']:
        cur = class_ptr
        if label == 'meta':
            cur = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, class_ptr)[0]
            if cur == 0 or cur >= len(data): break
        
        ro_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, cur + 32)[0]
        if ro_ptr == 0 or ro_ptr >= len(data): continue
        
        methods_vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, ro_ptr + 32)[0]
        if methods_vmaddr < linkedit_vmaddr: continue
        
        # This method list is in our new area
        methods_fileoff = linkedit_fileoff + (methods_vmaddr - linkedit_vmaddr)
        if methods_fileoff >= len(data): continue
        
        flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_fileoff)[0]
        count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_fileoff + 4)[0]
        
        if flags & 0x80000000:
            print(f'WARNING: method list at 0x{methods_fileoff:x} still has small flag!')
            continue
        
        # Add rebase entries for each method's 3 pointer fields
        for j in range(count):
            entry_fileoff = methods_fileoff + 8 + j * 24
            entry_vmaddr = methods_vmaddr + 8 + j * 24
            off_in_seg = entry_vmaddr - linkedit_vmaddr
            
            # name field at +0
            new_rebase_entries.append((seg_idx, off_in_seg))
            # types field at +8
            new_rebase_entries.append((seg_idx, off_in_seg + 8))
            # imp field at +16
            new_rebase_entries.append((seg_idx, off_in_seg + 16))

# Also check categories
catlist_off = 0x1c1b20
catlist_size = 0x8
for i in range(catlist_size // 8):
    cat_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, catlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    if cat_ptr == 0 or cat_ptr >= len(data): continue
    for moff_in_cat in [16, 24]:
        methods_vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, cat_ptr + moff_in_cat)[0]
        if methods_vmaddr < linkedit_vmaddr: continue
        methods_fileoff = linkedit_fileoff + (methods_vmaddr - linkedit_vmaddr)
        if methods_fileoff >= len(data): continue
        flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_fileoff)[0]
        count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_fileoff + 4)[0]
        if flags & 0x80000000: continue
        for j in range(count):
            off_in_seg = (methods_vmaddr - linkedit_vmaddr) + 8 + j * 24
            new_rebase_entries.append((seg_idx, off_in_seg))
            new_rebase_entries.append((seg_idx, off_in_seg + 8))
            new_rebase_entries.append((seg_idx, off_in_seg + 16))

print(f'Need {len(new_rebase_entries)} new rebase entries')

# Build new rebase opcode stream = old rebase opcodes (minus DONE) + new entries + DONE
# Strip the DONE byte from old rebase data
if old_rebase[-1] == 0x00:
    old_rebase = old_rebase[:-1]

# Generate new rebase opcodes
def uleb128(v):
    result = bytearray()
    while True:
        byte = v & 0x7F
        v >>= 7
        if v: byte |= 0x80
        result.append(byte)
        if not v: break
    return bytes(result)

new_ops = bytearray()
for seg, off_in_seg in sorted(new_rebase_entries):
    new_ops.append(0x20 | seg)  # REBASE_OPCODE_SET_SEGMENT_AND_OFFSET_ULEB | seg
    new_ops.extend(uleb128(off_in_seg))
    new_ops.append(0x51)  # REBASE_OPCODE_DO_REBASE_IMM_TIMES | 1

new_ops.append(0x00)  # REBASE_OPCODE_DONE

# Combine: old rebase (minus DONE) + new entries + DONE
combined_rebase = old_rebase + new_ops

# Now we need to place this new rebase data, the bind data, and update offsets
# The old rebase and bind data are at specific file offsets
# New approach: append new combined rebase + copy of bind data at end of file

# Align to 8 bytes
file_end = (len(data) + 7) & ~7
data.extend(b'\x00' * (file_end - len(data)))

new_rebase_foff = file_end
data.extend(combined_rebase)
# Pad to 8-byte alignment
while len(data) % 8 != 0:
    data.append(0)

new_bind_foff = len(data)
# Copy bind data from old location
old_bind_off = di_vals[4]
old_bind_size = di_vals[5]
data.extend(data[old_bind_off:old_bind_off + old_bind_size])

# Update LC_DYLD_INFO_ONLY
struct.pack_into('<I', data, di_off + 8, new_rebase_foff)  # rebase_off
struct.pack_into('<I', data, di_off + 12, len(combined_rebase))  # rebase_size
struct.pack_into('<I', data, di_off + 16, new_bind_foff)  # bind_off
struct.pack_into('<I', data, di_off + 20, old_bind_size)  # bind_size (unchanged)

print(f'New rebase: off=0x{new_rebase_foff:x} size={len(combined_rebase)}')
print(f'New bind: off=0x{new_bind_foff:x} size={old_bind_size}')

# Update __LINKEDIT segment
new_filesize = len(data) - linkedit_fileoff
new_vmsize = (new_filesize + 0xFFF) & ~0xFFF
struct.pack_into('<Q', data, linkedit_cmd_off + 32, new_vmsize)
struct.pack_into('<Q', data, linkedit_cmd_off + 48, new_filesize)
print(f'__LINKEDIT: filesize=0x{new_filesize:x} vmsize=0x{new_vmsize:x}')

with open('libFosterPlatform.dylib', 'wb') as f:
    f.write(data)
print(f'Wrote {len(data)} bytes')

# Start fresh approach: rebuild from the current binary
# Create a new writable segment for method lists

    data = bytearray(f.read())

# Parse current layout
off = 32
ncmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 16)[0]
sizeofcmds = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, 20)[0]
segs = []
di_off = None
linkedit_cmd_off = None

for i in range(ncmds):
    cmd, cmdsize = struct.unpack_from('<II', data, off)
    if cmd == 0x19:
        segname = data[off+8:off+24].split(b'\x00')[0].decode()
        vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+24)[0]
        vmsize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+32)[0]
        fileoff = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+40)[0]
        filesize = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, off+48)[0]
        segs.append({'name': segname, 'vmaddr': vmaddr, 'vmsize': vmsize, 
                     'fileoff': fileoff, 'filesize': filesize, 'cmd_off': off})
        if segname == '__LINKEDIT':
            linkedit_cmd_off = off
    elif cmd == 0x80000022:
        di_off = off
    off += cmdsize

print("Current segments:")
for s in segs:
    print(f"  {s['name']:16s} vm=0x{s['vmaddr']:x}+0x{s['vmsize']:x} file=0x{s['fileoff']:x}+0x{s['filesize']:x}")

# Current state: method lists are in extended __LINKEDIT (bad - read-only)
# We need to separate them into a new writable segment

# Step 1: Find all class_ro_t baseMethods pointers that point into __LINKEDIT
classlist_off = 0x1c1a98

li_vmaddr = linkedit_seg['vmaddr']
li_fileoff = linkedit_seg['fileoff']

method_lists_in_linkedit = []
for i in range(nclasses):
    class_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, classlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    if class_ptr == 0 or class_ptr >= len(data): continue
    
    for label in ['class', 'meta']:
        cur = class_ptr
        if label == 'meta':
            cur = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, class_ptr)[0]
            if cur == 0 or cur >= len(data): break
        
        ro_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, cur + 32)[0]
        if ro_ptr == 0 or ro_ptr >= len(data): continue
        
        methods_vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, ro_ptr + 32)[0]
        if methods_vmaddr >= li_vmaddr:
            methods_fileoff = li_fileoff + (methods_vmaddr - li_vmaddr)
            if methods_fileoff < len(data):
                flags = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_fileoff)[0]
                count = struct.unpack_from('<I', data, methods_fileoff + 4)[0]
                size = 8 + count * 24
                # Align
                size = (size + 7) & ~7
                method_lists_in_linkedit.append({
                    'ro_ptr_off': ro_ptr + 32,
                    'old_vmaddr': methods_vmaddr,
                    'fileoff': methods_fileoff,
                    'size': size,
                    'count': count
                })

# Also check categories
catlist_off = 0x1c1b20
for i in range(0x8 // 8):
    cat_ptr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, catlist_off + i * 8)[0]
    if cat_ptr == 0 or cat_ptr >= len(data): continue
    for moff in [16, 24]:
        methods_vmaddr = struct.unpack_from('<Q', data, cat_ptr + moff)[0]
        if methods_vmaddr >= li_vmaddr:

# Parse and rebuild rebase opcodes
def decode_uleb(buf, pos):
    result = 0; shift = 0
    while pos < len(buf):
        b = buf[pos]; pos += 1
        result |= (b & 0x7F) << shift
        if not (b & 0x80): break
        shift += 7
    return result, pos

def encode_uleb(v):
    result = bytearray()
    while True:
        byte = v & 0x7F; v >>= 7
        if v: byte |= 0x80
        result.append(byte)
        if not v: break
    return bytes(result)

# Parse current rebase opcodes
rebase_entries = []
pos = 0
cur_seg = 0; cur_off = 0; cur_type = 1
while pos < len(cur_rebase):
    byte = cur_rebase[pos]; pos += 1
    opcode = byte & 0xF0; imm = byte & 0x0F
    if opcode == 0x00: break
    elif opcode == 0x10: cur_type = imm
    elif opcode == 0x20:
        cur_seg = imm
        cur_off, pos = decode_uleb(cur_rebase, pos)
    elif opcode == 0x30:
        val, pos = decode_uleb(cur_rebase, pos)
        cur_off += val
    elif opcode == 0x40:
        cur_off += imm * 8
    elif opcode == 0x50:
        for _ in range(imm):
            rebase_entries.append((cur_type, cur_seg, cur_off))
            cur_off += 8
    elif opcode == 0x60:
        count, pos = decode_uleb(cur_rebase, pos)
        for _ in range(count):
            rebase_entries.append((cur_type, cur_seg, cur_off))
            cur_off += 8
    elif opcode == 0x70:
        skip, pos = decode_uleb(cur_rebase, pos)
        rebase_entries.append((cur_type, cur_seg, cur_off))
        cur_off += skip + 8
    elif opcode == 0x80:
        count, pos = decode_uleb(cur_rebase, pos)
        skip, pos = decode_uleb(cur_rebase, pos)
        for _ in range(count):
            rebase_entries.append((cur_type, cur_seg, cur_off))
            cur_off += skip + 8

print(f"Parsed {len(rebase_entries)} rebase entries from current data")

        if is_ml:
